=== Iteration 1 - [2025-08-28 02:15:50] ===
PLAN:
  Based on the provided hardware and environment information, which strongly indicates a containerized setup using Docker, the original plan requires significant adjustments to ensure feasibility. The following revised plan is tailored for an `x86_64` architecture using Docker containers on a Linux host, replacing physical multi-host dependencies with a simulated container network and a software switch model instead of hardware drivers.
  ***
  ### **ADJUSTED ENVIRONMENT SETUP PLAN**
  **Context:** This plan is adapted for a containerized environment managed by Docker. The "Switch Management Machine" and "Hosts" (Host1, Host2, Host3) will be run as separate Docker containers. The working directory `/home/cc/EnvGym/data/P4Ctl` is the Docker build context.
  1.  DOWNLOADS NEEDED:
      *   **Base Docker Image:** `ubuntu:22.04` (LTS). This is recommended over 20.04 to ensure a more recent host kernel is available, which is critical for eBPF/BCC compatibility with kernel versions like 5.15.0+. Docker containers share the host's kernel.
      *   **P4 Switch Software:** Tofino Switch SDE 9.7.0 (Requires access from Intel/Barefoot). For this containerized environment, we will use the **Tofino behavioral model (`modeld`)** included in the SDE, not the physical hardware driver (`switchd`).
      *   **eBPF Toolchain:** BCC (Bionic Compiler Collection). Must be compatible with the **host machine's Linux Kernel**.
      *   **Programming Language:** Python 3.7.
      *   **Python Libraries:** Scapy 2.4.5.
      *   **Compiler Tools:** Bison 3.8.2, Flex 2.6.4, `g++` (from `build-essential`), `libfl-dev`.
      *   **Networking Tools:** `ncat` (from `nmap`), `iproute2` (for `ip a`).
      *   **Source Code:** The P4Control project repository from `https://github.com/peng-gao-lab/p4control`.
  2.  FILES TO CREATE/MODIFY (Within the Container Filesystem):
      *   **File to Modify:** `host_agent/host_agent.py`
          *   **Path:** Within the cloned `p4control` repository, on each of the three "host" containers.
          *   **Description:** This file must be edited to specify the correct network interface name. In a standard Docker container network, this is typically **`"eth0"`**. Search for the interface name variable and update its value accordingly.
      *   **File to Modify (Dynamically):** `host_agent/host_agent_ebpf.c`
          *   **Path:** Within the cloned `p4control` repository, on each of the three "host" containers.
          *   **Description:** Before running the host agent, the `TAGGED_TERMINAL` macro must be updated with the PID of the shell process *inside the specific container*. This is found by running `ps` after attaching to the container's shell.
      *   **File to Modify (for Custom Policies):** `switch/netcl.py`
          *   **Path:** Within the cloned `p4control` repository, in the "switch" container.
          *   **Description:** To apply custom network policies, compile them using the `netcl-compile` tool. The output must be copied into this Python file, replacing the existing rules.
      *   **File to Create (Executable):** `compiler/netcl-compile`
          *   **Path:** Within the cloned `p4control` repository, in the `compiler/` subdirectory inside the "switch" container.
          *   **Description:** This compiler executable is built from source using the provided Makefile. It must be built before the switch controller can be run with custom policies.
  3.  NECESSARY TEST CASES IN THE CODEBASE:
      *   **(No changes)** The logic of the test cases remains the same, but they will be executed between containers on a Docker network instead of between physical hosts.
  4.  COMPLETE TODO LIST:
      *   **Phase 1: Docker Image and Environment Preparation (On Host Machine)**
          1.  **Create a Dockerfile:** In a new directory, create a `Dockerfile` to build a base image with all common dependencies.
              ```Dockerfile
              # Use Ubuntu 22.04 for better kernel compatibility for eBPF
              FROM ubuntu:22.04
              # Avoid interactive prompts during build
              ENV DEBIAN_FRONTEND=noninteractive
              # Install common dependencies and add repository for Python 3.7
              RUN apt-get update && \
                  apt-get install -y software-properties-common && \
                  add-apt-repository ppa:deadsnakes/ppa && \
                  apt-get update && \
                  apt-get install -y git python3.7 python3.7-distutils python3.7-dev nmap build-essential libfl-dev iproute2 curl && \
                  rm -rf /var/lib/apt/lists/*
              # Install pip for Python 3.7
              RUN curl https://bootstrap.pypa.io/get-pip.py -o get-pip.py && \
                  python3.7 get-pip.py && \
                  rm get-pip.py
              # Install required Python library
              RUN python3.7 -m pip install scapy==2.4.5
              # Set a working directory
              WORKDIR /root
              ```
          2.  **Build the Base Docker Image:**
              ```bash
              docker build -t p4control-base .
              ```
          3.  **Prepare Project and SDE:**
              *   Clone the P4Control project into the build context directory: `git clone https://github.com/peng-gao-lab/p4control /home/cc/EnvGym/data/P4Ctl`.
              *   Download and extract the Tofino SDE 9.7.0 into the build context as well, so it can be copied into the switch container.
          4.  **Create Docker Network:** Create a dedicated network for the containers to communicate.
              ```bash
              docker network create --subnet=10.0.0.0/24 p4control-net
              ```
      *   **Phase 2: Launch Containers**
          1.  **Launch the Switch Container:** This container will run the Tofino model and the controller.
              ```bash
              docker run -itd --name p4switch --net p4control-net -v /home/cc/EnvGym/data/P4Ctl:/root/p4control --cap-add=ALL --privileged p4control-base
              ```
          2.  **Launch the Host Containers:**
              ```bash
              docker run -itd --name host1 --net p4control-net --ip 10.0.0.1 -v /home/cc/EnvGym/data/P4Ctl:/root/p4control --cap-add=ALL --privileged p4control-base
              docker run -itd --name host2 --net p4control-net --ip 10.0.0.2 -v /home/cc/EnvGym/data/P4Ctl:/root/p4control --cap-add=ALL --privileged p4control-base
              docker run -itd --name host3 --net p4control-net --ip 10.0.0.3 -v /home/cc/EnvGym/data/P4Ctl:/root/p4control --cap-add=ALL --privileged p4control-base
              ```
          3.  **Verification:**
              ```bash
              docker ps # Should show p4switch, host1, host2, and host3 running
              ```
      *   **Phase 3: Tofino SDE and Host Environment Setup**
          1.  **On the Switch Container (`p4switch`):**
              *   Copy the SDE into the container (if not mounted via volume) and install it according to vendor instructions.
              *   Set environment variables. It's best to do this by attaching to the container:
                  ```bash
                  docker exec -it p4switch bash
                  # Inside the container:
                  echo 'export SDE=/path/to/bf-sde-9.7.0/' >> ~/.bashrc
                  echo 'export SDE_INSTALL=/path/to/bf-sde-9.7.0/install' >> ~/.bashrc
                  source ~/.bashrc
                  exit
                  ```
          2.  **On Each Host Container (`host1`, `host2`, `host3`):**
              *   Attach to the container: `docker exec -it <container_name> bash`.
              *   Install build tools (Bison, Flex) and BCC as described in the original plan. The host's kernel must be compatible.
              *   Configure Host Agent: Edit `/root/p4control/host_agent/host_agent.py` and set the interface name to `"eth0"`.
      *   **Phase 4: Build P4 Program and Start Switch Simulator (in `p4switch` container)**
          1.  Attach to the switch container: `docker exec -it p4switch bash`.
          2.  Navigate to the project directory: `cd /root/p4control`.
          3.  Build the P4 program: `./p4_build.sh -p switch/p4control.p4`.
          4.  Run the **Tofino behavioral model** in the background.
              ```bash
              ./run_tofino_model.sh -p p4control &
              ```
          5.  **Verification:** The model should be running without errors.
      *   **Phase 5: Compile Policy and Run Controller (in `p4switch` container)**
          1.  While still inside the `p4switch` container, navigate to `compiler`: `cd compiler`.
          2.  Build the policy compiler: `make netcl`.
          3.  Compile the policy and copy the output rules.
          4.  Paste the new rules into `switch/netcl.py`.
          5.  Navigate to the project root and start the controller:
              ```bash
              cd ..
              python3.7 switch/controller.py
              ```
          6.  **Verification:** The controller should log its connection to the switch model and the insertion of rules.
      *   **Phase 6: Deploy Host Agents (in `host1`, `host2`, `host3` containers)**
          1.  For each host container (e.g., `host1`):
              *   Attach an interactive shell: `docker exec -it host1 bash`.
              *   Get the PID of this shell: `ps`. Note the PID for the `bash` process.
              *   Edit `/root/p4control/host_agent/host_agent_ebpf.c` and set `TAGGED_TERMINAL` to this PID.
              *   In the same shell, run the agent: `sudo python3.7 host_agent/host_agent.py`.
          2.  **Verification:** The agent should start without eBPF compilation or attachment errors.
          3.  Repeat this process for `host2` and `host3` in separate terminal windows.
      *   **Phase 7: Execute Verification Test Case**
          1.  **On Host2 and Host3:** In the shells where the agents are running, start `ncat` listeners.
              ```bash
              # In host2's attached shell
              sudo ncat -nlvp 9999 -e /bin/bash
              # In host3's attached shell
              sudo ncat -nlvp 9999 -e /bin/bash
              ```
          2.  **On Host1:** In its attached shell, connect to Host2.
              ```bash
              sudo ncat 10.0.0.2 9999
              ```
          3.  **Verification:** You should get a shell prompt from Host2 inside the Host1 terminal.
          4.  **From the session on Host1 (now connected to Host2):** Attempt to connect to Host3.
              ```bash
              ncat 10.0.0.3 9999
              ```
          5.  **Final Verification:** This connection must fail (hang or timeout). This confirms the P4Control policy, enforced by the Tofino model, has correctly blocked the prohibited information flow between containers.
NEXT:
  current progress
  The previous Docker build failure, caused by a syntax error in a multi-line `apt-get` command, has been resolved by restructuring the `RUN` instructions in the current Dockerfile. The new Dockerfile is a comprehensive, single-stage build that successfully installs all specified system dependencies (including eBPF/BCC tools), Python packages, clones the project repository, and pre-builds the `netcl` policy compiler. The process for integrating the proprietary Tofino SDE has been prepared with commented-out instructions, marking the completion of the automated dependency setup.
  next step
  Download the Tofino SDE 9.7.0 archive (`bf-sde-9.7.0.tar.gz`) and place it in the same directory as the Dockerfile. Then, uncomment the `COPY` and `RUN` commands in the Dockerfile that handle the SDE's integration. After uncommenting these lines, rebuild the Docker image.

  #5 25.50 Supported Ubuntu and Python Versions
  #5 25.50 ====================================
  #5 25.50 
  #5 25.50 - Ubuntu 20.04 (focal) Python3.5 - Python3.7, Python3.9 - Python3.13
  #5 25.50 - Ubuntu 22.04 (jammy) Python3.7 - Python3.9, Python3.11 - Python3.13
  #5 25.50 - Ubuntu 24.04 (noble) Python3.7 - Python3.11, Python3.13
  #5 25.50 - Note: Python2.7 (focal, jammy), Python 3.8 (focal), Python 3.10 (jammy), Python3.12 (noble) are not provided by deadsnakes as upstream ubuntu provides those packages.
  #5 25.50 
  #5 25.50 Why some packages aren't built:
  #5 25.50 - Note: for focal, older python versions require libssl<1.1 so they are not currently built
  #5 25.50 - Note: for jammy and noble, older python versions requre libssl<3 so they are not currently built
  #5 25.50 - If you need these, reach out to asottile to set up a private ppa
  #5 25.50 
  #5 25.50 The packages may also work on other versions of Ubuntu or Debian, but that is not tested or supported.
  #5 25.50 
  #5 25.50 Packages
  #5 25.50 ========
  #5 25.50 
  #5 25.50 The packages provided here are loosely based on the debian upstream packages with some modifications to make them more usable as non-default pythons and on ubuntu.  As such, the packages follow debian's patterns and often do not include a full python distribution with just `apt install python#.#`.  Here is a list of packages that may be useful along with the default install:
  #5 25.50 
  #5 25.50 - `python#.#-dev`: includes development headers for building C extensions
  #5 25.50 - `python#.#-venv`: provides the standard library `venv` module
  #5 25.50 - `python#.#-distutils`: provides the standard library `distutils` module
  #5 25.50 - `python#.#-lib2to3`: provides the `2to3-#.#` utility as well as the standard library `lib2to3` module
  #5 25.50 - `python#.#-gdbm`: provides the standard library `dbm.gnu` module
  #5 25.50 - `python#.#-tk`: provides the standard library `tkinter` module
  #5 25.50 
  #5 25.50 Third-Party Python Modules
  #5 25.50 ==========================
  #5 25.50 
  #5 25.50 Python modules in the official Ubuntu repositories are packaged to work with the Python interpreters from the official repositories. Accordingly, they generally won't work with the Python interpreters from this PPA. As an exception, pure-Python modules for Python 3 will work, but any compiled extension modules won't.
  #5 25.50 
  #5 25.50 To install 3rd-party Python modules, you should use the common Python packaging tools.  For an introduction into the Python packaging ecosystem and its tools, refer to the Python Packaging User Guide:
  #5 25.50 https://packaging.python.org/installing/
  #5 25.50

DOCKERFILE:
  # Use Ubuntu 22.04 for better kernel compatibility for eBPF
  FROM ubuntu:22.04
  # Avoid interactive prompts during build
  ENV DEBIAN_FRONTEND=noninteractive
  # Set environment variables for Tofino SDE for consistency with the plan
  # These paths will be used if the SDE is installed.
  ENV SDE=/root/bf-sde-9.7.0
  ENV SDE_INSTALL=${SDE}/install
  # Install system dependencies, Python 3.7, build tools, and eBPF/BCC libraries
  RUN apt-get update && \
      apt-get install -y --no-install-recommends \
      # For adding PPA repository
      software-properties-common \
      # Version control and networking tools
      git \
      curl \
      nmap \
      iproute2 \
      # Build essentials and compiler tools
      build-essential \
      bison \
      flex \
      libfl-dev \
      # eBPF/BCC tools. bpfcc-tools provides a good base for Ubuntu 22.04.
      # Note: Full eBPF functionality depends on the host kernel version and headers.
      bpfcc-tools \
      libbpfcc-dev \
      # Add PPA for Python 3.7
      && add-apt-repository ppa:deadsnakes/ppa && \
      apt-get update && \
      # Install Python 3.7 and its development files
      apt-get install -y --no-install-recommends python3.7 python3.7-distutils python3.7-dev && \
      # Clean up APT cache to reduce image size
      apt-get clean && \
      rm -rf /var/lib/apt/lists/*
  # Install pip for Python 3.7
  RUN curl https://bootstrap.pypa.io/get-pip.py -o get-pip.py && \
      python3.7 get-pip.py && \
      rm get-pip.py
  # Install required Python libraries
  RUN python3.7 -m pip install --no-cache-dir scapy==2.4.5
  # Clone the P4Control project repository
  RUN git clone https://github.com/peng-gao-lab/p4control.git /root/p4control
  # Set the working directory to the root of the cloned repository
  WORKDIR /root/p4control
  # Build the netcl policy compiler as specified in the plan
  RUN cd compiler && make netcl
  # --- Tofino SDE Installation (Manual Step Required) ---
  # The Tofino SDE is proprietary software required to build and run the P4 switch program.
  # It cannot be downloaded automatically.
  #
  # INSTRUCTIONS FOR USER:
  # 1. Download the Tofino SDE 9.7.0 archive (e.g., 'bf-sde-9.7.0.tar.gz').
  # 2. Place the archive in the same directory as this Dockerfile (the build context).
  # 3. Uncomment the following lines to copy and set up the SDE during the image build.
  # COPY bf-sde-9.7.0.tar.gz /root/
  # RUN cd /root && \
  #     tar -xzf bf-sde-9.7.0.tar.gz && \
  #     rm bf-sde-9.7.0.tar.gz && \
  #     cd ${SDE} && \
  #     ./p4studio_build/p4studio_build.py --use-profile p416_examples.pro --setup-only
  # Start a bash shell when the container is run, placing the user in the WORKDIR
  CMD ["/bin/bash"]
--- End of Iteration 1 ---

=== Iteration 2 - [2025-08-28 02:17:00] ===
PLAN:
  Based on the provided hardware and environment information, which strongly indicates a containerized setup using Docker, the original plan requires significant adjustments to ensure feasibility. The following revised plan is tailored for an `x86_64` architecture using Docker containers on a Linux host, replacing physical multi-host dependencies with a simulated container network and a software switch model instead of hardware drivers.
  ***
  ### **ADJUSTED ENVIRONMENT SETUP PLAN**
  **Context:** This plan is adapted for a containerized environment managed by Docker. The "Switch Management Machine" and "Hosts" (Host1, Host2, Host3) will be run as separate Docker containers. The working directory `/home/cc/EnvGym/data/P4Ctl` is the Docker build context.
  1.  DOWNLOADS NEEDED:
      *   **Base Docker Image:** `ubuntu:22.04` (LTS). This is recommended over 20.04 to ensure a more recent host kernel is available, which is critical for eBPF/BCC compatibility with kernel versions like 5.15.0+. Docker containers share the host's kernel.
      *   **P4 Switch Software:** Tofino Switch SDE 9.7.0 (Requires access from Intel/Barefoot). For this containerized environment, we will use the **Tofino behavioral model (`modeld`)** included in the SDE, not the physical hardware driver (`switchd`).
      *   **eBPF Toolchain:** BCC (Bionic Compiler Collection). Must be compatible with the **host machine's Linux Kernel**.
      *   **Programming Language:** Python 3.7.
      *   **Python Libraries:** Scapy 2.4.5.
      *   **Compiler Tools:** Bison 3.8.2, Flex 2.6.4, `g++` (from `build-essential`), `libfl-dev`.
      *   **Networking Tools:** `ncat` (from `nmap`), `iproute2` (for `ip a`).
      *   **Source Code:** The P4Control project repository from `https://github.com/peng-gao-lab/p4control`.
  2.  FILES TO CREATE/MODIFY (Within the Container Filesystem):
      *   **File to Modify:** `host_agent/host_agent.py`
          *   **Path:** Within the cloned `p4control` repository, on each of the three "host" containers.
          *   **Description:** This file must be edited to specify the correct network interface name. In a standard Docker container network, this is typically **`"eth0"`**. Search for the interface name variable and update its value accordingly.
      *   **File to Modify (Dynamically):** `host_agent/host_agent_ebpf.c`
          *   **Path:** Within the cloned `p4control` repository, on each of the three "host" containers.
          *   **Description:** Before running the host agent, the `TAGGED_TERMINAL` macro must be updated with the PID of the shell process *inside the specific container*. This is found by running `ps` after attaching to the container's shell.
      *   **File to Modify (for Custom Policies):** `switch/netcl.py`
          *   **Path:** Within the cloned `p4control` repository, in the "switch" container.
          *   **Description:** To apply custom network policies, compile them using the `netcl-compile` tool. The output must be copied into this Python file, replacing the existing rules.
      *   **File to Create (Executable):** `compiler/netcl-compile`
          *   **Path:** Within the cloned `p4control` repository, in the `compiler/` subdirectory inside the "switch" container.
          *   **Description:** This compiler executable is built from source using the provided Makefile. It must be built before the switch controller can be run with custom policies.
  3.  NECESSARY TEST CASES IN THE CODEBASE:
      *   **(No changes)** The logic of the test cases remains the same, but they will be executed between containers on a Docker network instead of between physical hosts.
  4.  COMPLETE TODO LIST:
      *   **Phase 1: Docker Image and Environment Preparation (On Host Machine)**
          1.  **Create a Dockerfile:** In a new directory, create a `Dockerfile` to build a base image with all common dependencies.
              ```Dockerfile
              # Use Ubuntu 22.04 for better kernel compatibility for eBPF
              FROM ubuntu:22.04
              # Avoid interactive prompts during build
              ENV DEBIAN_FRONTEND=noninteractive
              # Install common dependencies and add repository for Python 3.7
              RUN apt-get update && \
                  apt-get install -y software-properties-common && \
                  add-apt-repository ppa:deadsnakes/ppa && \
                  apt-get update && \
                  apt-get install -y git python3.7 python3.7-distutils python3.7-dev nmap build-essential libfl-dev iproute2 curl && \
                  rm -rf /var/lib/apt/lists/*
              # Install pip for Python 3.7
              RUN curl https://bootstrap.pypa.io/get-pip.py -o get-pip.py && \
                  python3.7 get-pip.py && \
                  rm get-pip.py
              # Install required Python library
              RUN python3.7 -m pip install scapy==2.4.5
              # Set a working directory
              WORKDIR /root
              ```
          2.  **Build the Base Docker Image:**
              ```bash
              docker build -t p4control-base .
              ```
          3.  **Prepare Project and SDE:**
              *   Clone the P4Control project into the build context directory: `git clone https://github.com/peng-gao-lab/p4control /home/cc/EnvGym/data/P4Ctl`.
              *   Download and extract the Tofino SDE 9.7.0 into the build context as well, so it can be copied into the switch container.
          4.  **Create Docker Network:** Create a dedicated network for the containers to communicate.
              ```bash
              docker network create --subnet=10.0.0.0/24 p4control-net
              ```
      *   **Phase 2: Launch Containers**
          1.  **Launch the Switch Container:** This container will run the Tofino model and the controller.
              ```bash
              docker run -itd --name p4switch --net p4control-net -v /home/cc/EnvGym/data/P4Ctl:/root/p4control --cap-add=ALL --privileged p4control-base
              ```
          2.  **Launch the Host Containers:**
              ```bash
              docker run -itd --name host1 --net p4control-net --ip 10.0.0.1 -v /home/cc/EnvGym/data/P4Ctl:/root/p4control --cap-add=ALL --privileged p4control-base
              docker run -itd --name host2 --net p4control-net --ip 10.0.0.2 -v /home/cc/EnvGym/data/P4Ctl:/root/p4control --cap-add=ALL --privileged p4control-base
              docker run -itd --name host3 --net p4control-net --ip 10.0.0.3 -v /home/cc/EnvGym/data/P4Ctl:/root/p4control --cap-add=ALL --privileged p4control-base
              ```
          3.  **Verification:**
              ```bash
              docker ps # Should show p4switch, host1, host2, and host3 running
              ```
      *   **Phase 3: Tofino SDE and Host Environment Setup**
          1.  **On the Switch Container (`p4switch`):**
              *   Copy the SDE into the container (if not mounted via volume) and install it according to vendor instructions.
              *   Set environment variables. It's best to do this by attaching to the container:
                  ```bash
                  docker exec -it p4switch bash
                  # Inside the container:
                  echo 'export SDE=/path/to/bf-sde-9.7.0/' >> ~/.bashrc
                  echo 'export SDE_INSTALL=/path/to/bf-sde-9.7.0/install' >> ~/.bashrc
                  source ~/.bashrc
                  exit
                  ```
          2.  **On Each Host Container (`host1`, `host2`, `host3`):**
              *   Attach to the container: `docker exec -it <container_name> bash`.
              *   Install build tools (Bison, Flex) and BCC as described in the original plan. The host's kernel must be compatible.
              *   Configure Host Agent: Edit `/root/p4control/host_agent/host_agent.py` and set the interface name to `"eth0"`.
      *   **Phase 4: Build P4 Program and Start Switch Simulator (in `p4switch` container)**
          1.  Attach to the switch container: `docker exec -it p4switch bash`.
          2.  Navigate to the project directory: `cd /root/p4control`.
          3.  Build the P4 program: `./p4_build.sh -p switch/p4control.p4`.
          4.  Run the **Tofino behavioral model** in the background.
              ```bash
              ./run_tofino_model.sh -p p4control &
              ```
          5.  **Verification:** The model should be running without errors.
      *   **Phase 5: Compile Policy and Run Controller (in `p4switch` container)**
          1.  While still inside the `p4switch` container, navigate to `compiler`: `cd compiler`.
          2.  Build the policy compiler: `make netcl`.
          3.  Compile the policy and copy the output rules.
          4.  Paste the new rules into `switch/netcl.py`.
          5.  Navigate to the project root and start the controller:
              ```bash
              cd ..
              python3.7 switch/controller.py
              ```
          6.  **Verification:** The controller should log its connection to the switch model and the insertion of rules.
      *   **Phase 6: Deploy Host Agents (in `host1`, `host2`, `host3` containers)**
          1.  For each host container (e.g., `host1`):
              *   Attach an interactive shell: `docker exec -it host1 bash`.
              *   Get the PID of this shell: `ps`. Note the PID for the `bash` process.
              *   Edit `/root/p4control/host_agent/host_agent_ebpf.c` and set `TAGGED_TERMINAL` to this PID.
              *   In the same shell, run the agent: `sudo python3.7 host_agent/host_agent.py`.
          2.  **Verification:** The agent should start without eBPF compilation or attachment errors.
          3.  Repeat this process for `host2` and `host3` in separate terminal windows.
      *   **Phase 7: Execute Verification Test Case**
          1.  **On Host2 and Host3:** In the shells where the agents are running, start `ncat` listeners.
              ```bash
              # In host2's attached shell
              sudo ncat -nlvp 9999 -e /bin/bash
              # In host3's attached shell
              sudo ncat -nlvp 9999 -e /bin/bash
              ```
          2.  **On Host1:** In its attached shell, connect to Host2.
              ```bash
              sudo ncat 10.0.0.2 9999
              ```
          3.  **Verification:** You should get a shell prompt from Host2 inside the Host1 terminal.
          4.  **From the session on Host1 (now connected to Host2):** Attempt to connect to Host3.
              ```bash
              ncat 10.0.0.3 9999
              ```
          5.  **Final Verification:** This connection must fail (hang or timeout). This confirms the P4Control policy, enforced by the Tofino model, has correctly blocked the prohibited information flow between containers.
NEXT:
  current progress
  The project is in Phase 1, attempting to build a unified Docker image for the environment. The Dockerfile successfully installs base dependencies, clones the project repository, and builds the `netcl` compiler. The build process failed at the Tofino SDE installation step because the required archive, `bf-sde-9.7.0.tar.gz`, was not found in the Docker build context. The current approach of building a single, monolithic image with the SDE included deviates from the original plan's more efficient strategy of creating a common base image.
  next step
  Modify the Dockerfile to align with the plan's intention of creating a reusable base image. Remove the entire Tofino SDE installation section. This will resolve the build failure and create a smaller, common base image for all host and switch containers. The SDE installation should be performed later, specifically within the `p4switch` container after it is launched, as detailed in Phase 3 of the plan.
  Delete the following lines from the Dockerfile:
  ```dockerfile
  # --- Tofino SDE Installation ---
  # Assumes 'bf-sde-9.7.0.tar.gz' is in the build context.
  COPY bf-sde-9.7.0.tar.gz /root/
  RUN cd /root && \
      tar -xzf bf-sde-9.7.0.tar.gz && \
      rm bf-sde-9.7.0.tar.gz && \
      cd ${SDE} && \
      ./p4studio_build/p4studio_build.py --use-profile p416_examples.pro --setup-only
  ```

DOCKERFILE:
  # Use Ubuntu 22.04 for better kernel compatibility for eBPF
  FROM ubuntu:22.04
  # Avoid interactive prompts during build
  ENV DEBIAN_FRONTEND=noninteractive
  # Set environment variables for Tofino SDE for consistency with the plan
  # These paths will be used if the SDE is installed.
  ENV SDE=/root/bf-sde-9.7.0
  ENV SDE_INSTALL=${SDE}/install
  # Install system dependencies, Python 3.7, build tools, and eBPF/BCC libraries
  RUN apt-get update && \
      apt-get install -y --no-install-recommends \
      # For adding PPA repository
      software-properties-common \
      # Version control and networking tools
      git \
      curl \
      nmap \
      iproute2 \
      # Build essentials and compiler tools
      build-essential \
      bison \
      flex \
      libfl-dev \
      # eBPF/BCC tools. bpfcc-tools provides a good base for Ubuntu 22.04.
      # Note: Full eBPF functionality depends on the host kernel version and headers.
      bpfcc-tools \
      libbpfcc-dev \
      # Add PPA for Python 3.7
      && add-apt-repository ppa:deadsnakes/ppa && \
      apt-get update && \
      # Install Python 3.7 and its development files
      apt-get install -y --no-install-recommends python3.7 python3.7-distutils python3.7-dev && \
      # Clean up APT cache to reduce image size
      apt-get clean && \
      rm -rf /var/lib/apt/lists/*
  # Install pip for Python 3.7
  RUN curl https://bootstrap.pypa.io/get-pip.py -o get-pip.py && \
      python3.7 get-pip.py && \
      rm get-pip.py
  # Install required Python libraries
  RUN python3.7 -m pip install --no-cache-dir scapy==2.4.5
  # Clone the P4Control project repository
  RUN git clone https://github.com/peng-gao-lab/p4control.git /root/p4control
  # Set the working directory to the root of the cloned repository
  WORKDIR /root/p4control
  # Build the netcl policy compiler as specified in the plan
  RUN cd compiler && make netcl
  # --- Tofino SDE Installation ---
  # Assumes 'bf-sde-9.7.0.tar.gz' is in the build context.
  COPY bf-sde-9.7.0.tar.gz /root/
  RUN cd /root && \
      tar -xzf bf-sde-9.7.0.tar.gz && \
      rm bf-sde-9.7.0.tar.gz && \
      cd ${SDE} && \
      ./p4studio_build/p4studio_build.py --use-profile p416_examples.pro --setup-only
  # Start a bash shell when the container is run, placing the user in the WORKDIR
  CMD ["/bin/bash"]
--- End of Iteration 2 ---

=== Iteration 3 - [2025-08-28 02:18:00] ===
PLAN:
  Based on the provided hardware and environment information, which strongly indicates a containerized setup using Docker, the original plan requires significant adjustments to ensure feasibility. The following revised plan is tailored for an `x86_64` architecture using Docker containers on a Linux host, replacing physical multi-host dependencies with a simulated container network and a software switch model instead of hardware drivers.
  ***
  ### **ADJUSTED ENVIRONMENT SETUP PLAN**
  **Context:** This plan is adapted for a containerized environment managed by Docker. The "Switch Management Machine" and "Hosts" (Host1, Host2, Host3) will be run as separate Docker containers. The working directory `/home/cc/EnvGym/data/P4Ctl` is the Docker build context.
  1.  DOWNLOADS NEEDED:
      *   **Base Docker Image:** `ubuntu:22.04` (LTS). This is recommended over 20.04 to ensure a more recent host kernel is available, which is critical for eBPF/BCC compatibility with kernel versions like 5.15.0+. Docker containers share the host's kernel.
      *   **P4 Switch Software:** Tofino Switch SDE 9.7.0 (Requires access from Intel/Barefoot). For this containerized environment, we will use the **Tofino behavioral model (`modeld`)** included in the SDE, not the physical hardware driver (`switchd`).
      *   **eBPF Toolchain:** BCC (Bionic Compiler Collection). Must be compatible with the **host machine's Linux Kernel**.
      *   **Programming Language:** Python 3.7.
      *   **Python Libraries:** Scapy 2.4.5.
      *   **Compiler Tools:** Bison 3.8.2, Flex 2.6.4, `g++` (from `build-essential`), `libfl-dev`.
      *   **Networking Tools:** `ncat` (from `nmap`), `iproute2` (for `ip a`).
      *   **Source Code:** The P4Control project repository from `https://github.com/peng-gao-lab/p4control`.
  2.  FILES TO CREATE/MODIFY (Within the Container Filesystem):
      *   **File to Modify:** `host_agent/host_agent.py`
          *   **Path:** Within the cloned `p4control` repository, on each of the three "host" containers.
          *   **Description:** This file must be edited to specify the correct network interface name. In a standard Docker container network, this is typically **`"eth0"`**. Search for the interface name variable and update its value accordingly.
      *   **File to Modify (Dynamically):** `host_agent/host_agent_ebpf.c`
          *   **Path:** Within the cloned `p4control` repository, on each of the three "host" containers.
          *   **Description:** Before running the host agent, the `TAGGED_TERMINAL` macro must be updated with the PID of the shell process *inside the specific container*. This is found by running `ps` after attaching to the container's shell.
      *   **File to Modify (for Custom Policies):** `switch/netcl.py`
          *   **Path:** Within the cloned `p4control` repository, in the "switch" container.
          *   **Description:** To apply custom network policies, compile them using the `netcl-compile` tool. The output must be copied into this Python file, replacing the existing rules.
      *   **File to Create (Executable):** `compiler/netcl-compile`
          *   **Path:** Within the cloned `p4control` repository, in the `compiler/` subdirectory inside the "switch" container.
          *   **Description:** This compiler executable is built from source using the provided Makefile. It must be built before the switch controller can be run with custom policies.
  3.  NECESSARY TEST CASES IN THE CODEBASE:
      *   **(No changes)** The logic of the test cases remains the same, but they will be executed between containers on a Docker network instead of between physical hosts.
  4.  COMPLETE TODO LIST:
      *   **Phase 1: Docker Image and Environment Preparation (On Host Machine)**
          1.  **Create a Dockerfile:** In a new directory, create a `Dockerfile` to build a base image with all common dependencies.
              ```Dockerfile
              # Use Ubuntu 22.04 for better kernel compatibility for eBPF
              FROM ubuntu:22.04
              # Avoid interactive prompts during build
              ENV DEBIAN_FRONTEND=noninteractive
              # Install common dependencies and add repository for Python 3.7
              RUN apt-get update && \
                  apt-get install -y software-properties-common && \
                  add-apt-repository ppa:deadsnakes/ppa && \
                  apt-get update && \
                  apt-get install -y git python3.7 python3.7-distutils python3.7-dev nmap build-essential libfl-dev iproute2 curl && \
                  rm -rf /var/lib/apt/lists/*
              # Install pip for Python 3.7
              RUN curl https://bootstrap.pypa.io/get-pip.py -o get-pip.py && \
                  python3.7 get-pip.py && \
                  rm get-pip.py
              # Install required Python library
              RUN python3.7 -m pip install scapy==2.4.5
              # Set a working directory
              WORKDIR /root
              ```
          2.  **Build the Base Docker Image:**
              ```bash
              docker build -t p4control-base .
              ```
          3.  **Prepare Project and SDE:**
              *   Clone the P4Control project into the build context directory: `git clone https://github.com/peng-gao-lab/p4control /home/cc/EnvGym/data/P4Ctl`.
              *   Download and extract the Tofino SDE 9.7.0 into the build context as well, so it can be copied into the switch container.
          4.  **Create Docker Network:** Create a dedicated network for the containers to communicate.
              ```bash
              docker network create --subnet=10.0.0.0/24 p4control-net
              ```
      *   **Phase 2: Launch Containers**
          1.  **Launch the Switch Container:** This container will run the Tofino model and the controller.
              ```bash
              docker run -itd --name p4switch --net p4control-net -v /home/cc/EnvGym/data/P4Ctl:/root/p4control --cap-add=ALL --privileged p4control-base
              ```
          2.  **Launch the Host Containers:**
              ```bash
              docker run -itd --name host1 --net p4control-net --ip 10.0.0.1 -v /home/cc/EnvGym/data/P4Ctl:/root/p4control --cap-add=ALL --privileged p4control-base
              docker run -itd --name host2 --net p4control-net --ip 10.0.0.2 -v /home/cc/EnvGym/data/P4Ctl:/root/p4control --cap-add=ALL --privileged p4control-base
              docker run -itd --name host3 --net p4control-net --ip 10.0.0.3 -v /home/cc/EnvGym/data/P4Ctl:/root/p4control --cap-add=ALL --privileged p4control-base
              ```
          3.  **Verification:**
              ```bash
              docker ps # Should show p4switch, host1, host2, and host3 running
              ```
      *   **Phase 3: Tofino SDE and Host Environment Setup**
          1.  **On the Switch Container (`p4switch`):**
              *   Copy the SDE into the container (if not mounted via volume) and install it according to vendor instructions.
              *   Set environment variables. It's best to do this by attaching to the container:
                  ```bash
                  docker exec -it p4switch bash
                  # Inside the container:
                  echo 'export SDE=/path/to/bf-sde-9.7.0/' >> ~/.bashrc
                  echo 'export SDE_INSTALL=/path/to/bf-sde-9.7.0/install' >> ~/.bashrc
                  source ~/.bashrc
                  exit
                  ```
          2.  **On Each Host Container (`host1`, `host2`, `host3`):**
              *   Attach to the container: `docker exec -it <container_name> bash`.
              *   Install build tools (Bison, Flex) and BCC as described in the original plan. The host's kernel must be compatible.
              *   Configure Host Agent: Edit `/root/p4control/host_agent/host_agent.py` and set the interface name to `"eth0"`.
      *   **Phase 4: Build P4 Program and Start Switch Simulator (in `p4switch` container)**
          1.  Attach to the switch container: `docker exec -it p4switch bash`.
          2.  Navigate to the project directory: `cd /root/p4control`.
          3.  Build the P4 program: `./p4_build.sh -p switch/p4control.p4`.
          4.  Run the **Tofino behavioral model** in the background.
              ```bash
              ./run_tofino_model.sh -p p4control &
              ```
          5.  **Verification:** The model should be running without errors.
      *   **Phase 5: Compile Policy and Run Controller (in `p4switch` container)**
          1.  While still inside the `p4switch` container, navigate to `compiler`: `cd compiler`.
          2.  Build the policy compiler: `make netcl`.
          3.  Compile the policy and copy the output rules.
          4.  Paste the new rules into `switch/netcl.py`.
          5.  Navigate to the project root and start the controller:
              ```bash
              cd ..
              python3.7 switch/controller.py
              ```
          6.  **Verification:** The controller should log its connection to the switch model and the insertion of rules.
      *   **Phase 6: Deploy Host Agents (in `host1`, `host2`, `host3` containers)**
          1.  For each host container (e.g., `host1`):
              *   Attach an interactive shell: `docker exec -it host1 bash`.
              *   Get the PID of this shell: `ps`. Note the PID for the `bash` process.
              *   Edit `/root/p4control/host_agent/host_agent_ebpf.c` and set `TAGGED_TERMINAL` to this PID.
              *   In the same shell, run the agent: `sudo python3.7 host_agent/host_agent.py`.
          2.  **Verification:** The agent should start without eBPF compilation or attachment errors.
          3.  Repeat this process for `host2` and `host3` in separate terminal windows.
      *   **Phase 7: Execute Verification Test Case**
          1.  **On Host2 and Host3:** In the shells where the agents are running, start `ncat` listeners.
              ```bash
              # In host2's attached shell
              sudo ncat -nlvp 9999 -e /bin/bash
              # In host3's attached shell
              sudo ncat -nlvp 9999 -e /bin/bash
              ```
          2.  **On Host1:** In its attached shell, connect to Host2.
              ```bash
              sudo ncat 10.0.0.2 9999
              ```
          3.  **Verification:** You should get a shell prompt from Host2 inside the Host1 terminal.
          4.  **From the session on Host1 (now connected to Host2):** Attempt to connect to Host3.
              ```bash
              ncat 10.0.0.3 9999
              ```
          5.  **Final Verification:** This connection must fail (hang or timeout). This confirms the P4Control policy, enforced by the Tofino model, has correctly blocked the prohibited information flow between containers.
NEXT:
  current progress
  The project has moved from a failed initial image build to a comprehensive, single Dockerfile. This file successfully automates the environment setup by installing all common system dependencies, Python 3.7, Scapy, and the BCC toolchain. It also clones the project repository and pre-builds the `netcl` policy compiler, completing several setup tasks originally planned to be done manually inside the running containers.
  next step
  Refactor the monolithic Dockerfile into a multi-stage build. Create a `base` stage with common dependencies, a `switch` target image that adds and installs the Tofino SDE, and a `host` target image with the necessary eBPF/BCC libraries. This will create optimized images for each container role as outlined in the plan, improving efficiency and separation of concerns.

  #5 28.52 
  #5 28.52 Supported Ubuntu and Python Versions
  #5 28.52 ====================================
  #5 28.52 
  #5 28.52 - Ubuntu 20.04 (focal) Python3.5 - Python3.7, Python3.9 - Python3.13
  #5 28.52 - Ubuntu 22.04 (jammy) Python3.7 - Python3.9, Python3.11 - Python3.13
  #5 28.52 - Ubuntu 24.04 (noble) Python3.7 - Python3.11, Python3.13
  #5 28.52 - Note: Python2.7 (focal, jammy), Python 3.8 (focal), Python 3.10 (jammy), Python3.12 (noble) are not provided by deadsnakes as upstream ubuntu provides those packages.
  #5 28.52 
  #5 28.52 Why some packages aren't built:
  #5 28.52 - Note: for focal, older python versions require libssl<1.1 so they are not currently built
  #5 28.52 - Note: for jammy and noble, older python versions requre libssl<3 so they are not currently built
  #5 28.52 - If you need these, reach out to asottile to set up a private ppa
  #5 28.52 
  #5 28.52 The packages may also work on other versions of Ubuntu or Debian, but that is not tested or supported.
  #5 28.52 
  #5 28.52 Packages
  #5 28.52 ========
  #5 28.52 
  #5 28.52 The packages provided here are loosely based on the debian upstream packages with some modifications to make them more usable as non-default pythons and on ubuntu.  As such, the packages follow debian's patterns and often do not include a full python distribution with just `apt install python#.#`.  Here is a list of packages that may be useful along with the default install:
  #5 28.52 
  #5 28.52 - `python#.#-dev`: includes development headers for building C extensions
  #5 28.52 - `python#.#-venv`: provides the standard library `venv` module
  #5 28.52 - `python#.#-distutils`: provides the standard library `distutils` module
  #5 28.52 - `python#.#-lib2to3`: provides the `2to3-#.#` utility as well as the standard library `lib2to3` module
  #5 28.52 - `python#.#-gdbm`: provides the standard library `dbm.gnu` module
  #5 28.52 - `python#.#-tk`: provides the standard library `tkinter` module
  #5 28.52 
  #5 28.52 Third-Party Python Modules
  #5 28.52 ==========================
  #5 28.52 
  #5 28.52 Python modules in the official Ubuntu repositories are packaged to work with the Python interpreters from the official repositories. Accordingly, they generally won't work with the Python interpreters from this PPA. As an exception, pure-Python modules for Python 3 will work, but any compiled extension modules won't.
  #5 28.52 
  #5 28.52 To install 3rd-party Python modules, you should use the common Python packaging tools.  For an introduction into the Python packaging ecosystem and its tools, refer to the Python Packaging User Guide:
  #5 28.52 https://packaging.python.org/installing/
  #5 28.52

DOCKERFILE:
  # Use Ubuntu 22.04 for better kernel compatibility for eBPF
  FROM ubuntu:22.04
  # Avoid interactive prompts during build
  ENV DEBIAN_FRONTEND=noninteractive
  # Set environment variables for Tofino SDE for consistency with the plan
  # These paths will be used if the SDE is installed.
  ENV SDE=/root/bf-sde-9.7.0
  ENV SDE_INSTALL=${SDE}/install
  # Install system dependencies, Python 3.7, build tools, and eBPF/BCC libraries
  RUN apt-get update && \
      apt-get install -y --no-install-recommends \
      # For adding PPA repository
      software-properties-common \
      # Version control and networking tools
      git \
      curl \
      nmap \
      iproute2 \
      # Build essentials and compiler tools
      build-essential \
      bison \
      flex \
      libfl-dev \
      # eBPF/BCC tools. bpfcc-tools provides a good base for Ubuntu 22.04.
      # Note: Full eBPF functionality depends on the host kernel version and headers.
      bpfcc-tools \
      libbpfcc-dev \
      # Add PPA for Python 3.7
      && add-apt-repository ppa:deadsnakes/ppa && \
      apt-get update && \
      # Install Python 3.7 and its development files
      apt-get install -y --no-install-recommends python3.7 python3.7-distutils python3.7-dev && \
      # Clean up APT cache to reduce image size
      apt-get clean && \
      rm -rf /var/lib/apt/lists/*
  # Install pip for Python 3.7
  RUN curl https://bootstrap.pypa.io/get-pip.py -o get-pip.py && \
      python3.7 get-pip.py && \
      rm get-pip.py
  # Install required Python libraries
  RUN python3.7 -m pip install --no-cache-dir scapy==2.4.5
  # Clone the P4Control project repository
  RUN git clone https://github.com/peng-gao-lab/p4control.git /root/p4control
  # Set the working directory to the root of the cloned repository
  WORKDIR /root/p4control
  # Build the netcl policy compiler as specified in the plan
  RUN cd compiler && make netcl
  # Start a bash shell when the container is run, placing the user in the WORKDIR
  CMD ["/bin/bash"]
--- End of Iteration 3 ---

=== Iteration 4 - [2025-08-28 02:19:33] ===
PLAN:
  Based on the provided hardware and environment information, which strongly indicates a containerized setup using Docker, the original plan requires significant adjustments to ensure feasibility. The following revised plan is tailored for an `x86_64` architecture using Docker containers on a Linux host, replacing physical multi-host dependencies with a simulated container network and a software switch model instead of hardware drivers.
  ***
  ### **ADJUSTED ENVIRONMENT SETUP PLAN**
  **Context:** This plan is adapted for a containerized environment managed by Docker. The "Switch Management Machine" and "Hosts" (Host1, Host2, Host3) will be run as separate Docker containers. The working directory `/home/cc/EnvGym/data/P4Ctl` is the Docker build context.
  1.  DOWNLOADS NEEDED:
      *   **Base Docker Image:** `ubuntu:22.04` (LTS). This is recommended over 20.04 to ensure a more recent host kernel is available, which is critical for eBPF/BCC compatibility with kernel versions like 5.15.0+. Docker containers share the host's kernel.
      *   **P4 Switch Software:** Tofino Switch SDE 9.7.0 (Requires access from Intel/Barefoot). For this containerized environment, we will use the **Tofino behavioral model (`modeld`)** included in the SDE, not the physical hardware driver (`switchd`).
      *   **eBPF Toolchain:** BCC (Bionic Compiler Collection). Must be compatible with the **host machine's Linux Kernel**.
      *   **Programming Language:** Python 3.7.
      *   **Python Libraries:** Scapy 2.4.5.
      *   **Compiler Tools:** Bison 3.8.2, Flex 2.6.4, `g++` (from `build-essential`), `libfl-dev`.
      *   **Networking Tools:** `ncat` (from `nmap`), `iproute2` (for `ip a`).
      *   **Source Code:** The P4Control project repository from `https://github.com/peng-gao-lab/p4control`.
  2.  FILES TO CREATE/MODIFY (Within the Container Filesystem):
      *   **File to Modify:** `host_agent/host_agent.py`
          *   **Path:** Within the cloned `p4control` repository, on each of the three "host" containers.
          *   **Description:** This file must be edited to specify the correct network interface name. In a standard Docker container network, this is typically **`"eth0"`**. Search for the interface name variable and update its value accordingly.
      *   **File to Modify (Dynamically):** `host_agent/host_agent_ebpf.c`
          *   **Path:** Within the cloned `p4control` repository, on each of the three "host" containers.
          *   **Description:** Before running the host agent, the `TAGGED_TERMINAL` macro must be updated with the PID of the shell process *inside the specific container*. This is found by running `ps` after attaching to the container's shell.
      *   **File to Modify (for Custom Policies):** `switch/netcl.py`
          *   **Path:** Within the cloned `p4control` repository, in the "switch" container.
          *   **Description:** To apply custom network policies, compile them using the `netcl-compile` tool. The output must be copied into this Python file, replacing the existing rules.
      *   **File to Create (Executable):** `compiler/netcl-compile`
          *   **Path:** Within the cloned `p4control` repository, in the `compiler/` subdirectory inside the "switch" container.
          *   **Description:** This compiler executable is built from source using the provided Makefile. It must be built before the switch controller can be run with custom policies.
  3.  NECESSARY TEST CASES IN THE CODEBASE:
      *   **(No changes)** The logic of the test cases remains the same, but they will be executed between containers on a Docker network instead of between physical hosts.
  4.  COMPLETE TODO LIST:
      *   **Phase 1: Docker Image and Environment Preparation (On Host Machine)**
          1.  **Create a Dockerfile:** In a new directory, create a `Dockerfile` to build a base image with all common dependencies.
              ```Dockerfile
              # Use Ubuntu 22.04 for better kernel compatibility for eBPF
              FROM ubuntu:22.04
              # Avoid interactive prompts during build
              ENV DEBIAN_FRONTEND=noninteractive
              # Install common dependencies and add repository for Python 3.7
              RUN apt-get update && \
                  apt-get install -y software-properties-common && \
                  add-apt-repository ppa:deadsnakes/ppa && \
                  apt-get update && \
                  apt-get install -y git python3.7 python3.7-distutils python3.7-dev nmap build-essential libfl-dev iproute2 curl && \
                  rm -rf /var/lib/apt/lists/*
              # Install pip for Python 3.7
              RUN curl https://bootstrap.pypa.io/get-pip.py -o get-pip.py && \
                  python3.7 get-pip.py && \
                  rm get-pip.py
              # Install required Python library
              RUN python3.7 -m pip install scapy==2.4.5
              # Set a working directory
              WORKDIR /root
              ```
          2.  **Build the Base Docker Image:**
              ```bash
              docker build -t p4control-base .
              ```
          3.  **Prepare Project and SDE:**
              *   Clone the P4Control project into the build context directory: `git clone https://github.com/peng-gao-lab/p4control /home/cc/EnvGym/data/P4Ctl`.
              *   Download and extract the Tofino SDE 9.7.0 into the build context as well, so it can be copied into the switch container.
          4.  **Create Docker Network:** Create a dedicated network for the containers to communicate.
              ```bash
              docker network create --subnet=10.0.0.0/24 p4control-net
              ```
      *   **Phase 2: Launch Containers**
          1.  **Launch the Switch Container:** This container will run the Tofino model and the controller.
              ```bash
              docker run -itd --name p4switch --net p4control-net -v /home/cc/EnvGym/data/P4Ctl:/root/p4control --cap-add=ALL --privileged p4control-base
              ```
          2.  **Launch the Host Containers:**
              ```bash
              docker run -itd --name host1 --net p4control-net --ip 10.0.0.1 -v /home/cc/EnvGym/data/P4Ctl:/root/p4control --cap-add=ALL --privileged p4control-base
              docker run -itd --name host2 --net p4control-net --ip 10.0.0.2 -v /home/cc/EnvGym/data/P4Ctl:/root/p4control --cap-add=ALL --privileged p4control-base
              docker run -itd --name host3 --net p4control-net --ip 10.0.0.3 -v /home/cc/EnvGym/data/P4Ctl:/root/p4control --cap-add=ALL --privileged p4control-base
              ```
          3.  **Verification:**
              ```bash
              docker ps # Should show p4switch, host1, host2, and host3 running
              ```
      *   **Phase 3: Tofino SDE and Host Environment Setup**
          1.  **On the Switch Container (`p4switch`):**
              *   Copy the SDE into the container (if not mounted via volume) and install it according to vendor instructions.
              *   Set environment variables. It's best to do this by attaching to the container:
                  ```bash
                  docker exec -it p4switch bash
                  # Inside the container:
                  echo 'export SDE=/path/to/bf-sde-9.7.0/' >> ~/.bashrc
                  echo 'export SDE_INSTALL=/path/to/bf-sde-9.7.0/install' >> ~/.bashrc
                  source ~/.bashrc
                  exit
                  ```
          2.  **On Each Host Container (`host1`, `host2`, `host3`):**
              *   Attach to the container: `docker exec -it <container_name> bash`.
              *   Install build tools (Bison, Flex) and BCC as described in the original plan. The host's kernel must be compatible.
              *   Configure Host Agent: Edit `/root/p4control/host_agent/host_agent.py` and set the interface name to `"eth0"`.
      *   **Phase 4: Build P4 Program and Start Switch Simulator (in `p4switch` container)**
          1.  Attach to the switch container: `docker exec -it p4switch bash`.
          2.  Navigate to the project directory: `cd /root/p4control`.
          3.  Build the P4 program: `./p4_build.sh -p switch/p4control.p4`.
          4.  Run the **Tofino behavioral model** in the background.
              ```bash
              ./run_tofino_model.sh -p p4control &
              ```
          5.  **Verification:** The model should be running without errors.
      *   **Phase 5: Compile Policy and Run Controller (in `p4switch` container)**
          1.  While still inside the `p4switch` container, navigate to `compiler`: `cd compiler`.
          2.  Build the policy compiler: `make netcl`.
          3.  Compile the policy and copy the output rules.
          4.  Paste the new rules into `switch/netcl.py`.
          5.  Navigate to the project root and start the controller:
              ```bash
              cd ..
              python3.7 switch/controller.py
              ```
          6.  **Verification:** The controller should log its connection to the switch model and the insertion of rules.
      *   **Phase 6: Deploy Host Agents (in `host1`, `host2`, `host3` containers)**
          1.  For each host container (e.g., `host1`):
              *   Attach an interactive shell: `docker exec -it host1 bash`.
              *   Get the PID of this shell: `ps`. Note the PID for the `bash` process.
              *   Edit `/root/p4control/host_agent/host_agent_ebpf.c` and set `TAGGED_TERMINAL` to this PID.
              *   In the same shell, run the agent: `sudo python3.7 host_agent/host_agent.py`.
          2.  **Verification:** The agent should start without eBPF compilation or attachment errors.
          3.  Repeat this process for `host2` and `host3` in separate terminal windows.
      *   **Phase 7: Execute Verification Test Case**
          1.  **On Host2 and Host3:** In the shells where the agents are running, start `ncat` listeners.
              ```bash
              # In host2's attached shell
              sudo ncat -nlvp 9999 -e /bin/bash
              # In host3's attached shell
              sudo ncat -nlvp 9999 -e /bin/bash
              ```
          2.  **On Host1:** In its attached shell, connect to Host2.
              ```bash
              sudo ncat 10.0.0.2 9999
              ```
          3.  **Verification:** You should get a shell prompt from Host2 inside the Host1 terminal.
          4.  **From the session on Host1 (now connected to Host2):** Attempt to connect to Host3.
              ```bash
              ncat 10.0.0.3 9999
              ```
          5.  **Final Verification:** This connection must fail (hang or timeout). This confirms the P4Control policy, enforced by the Tofino model, has correctly blocked the prohibited information flow between containers.

  #6 24.87 Reporting Issues
  #6 24.87 ================
  #6 24.87 
  #6 24.87 Issues can be reported in the master issue tracker at:
  #6 24.87 https://github.com/deadsnakes/issues/issues
  #6 24.87 
  #6 24.87 Supported Ubuntu and Python Versions
  #6 24.87 ====================================
  #6 24.87 
  #6 24.87 - Ubuntu 20.04 (focal) Python3.5 - Python3.7, Python3.9 - Python3.13
  #6 24.87 - Ubuntu 22.04 (jammy) Python3.7 - Python3.9, Python3.11 - Python3.13
  #6 24.87 - Ubuntu 24.04 (noble) Python3.7 - Python3.11, Python3.13
  #6 24.87 - Note: Python2.7 (focal, jammy), Python 3.8 (focal), Python 3.10 (jammy), Python3.12 (noble) are not provided by deadsnakes as upstream ubuntu provides those packages.
  #6 24.87 
  #6 24.87 Why some packages aren't built:
  #6 24.87 - Note: for focal, older python versions require libssl<1.1 so they are not currently built
  #6 24.87 - Note: for jammy and noble, older python versions requre libssl<3 so they are not currently built
  #6 24.87 - If you need these, reach out to asottile to set up a private ppa
  #6 24.87 
  #6 24.87 The packages may also work on other versions of Ubuntu or Debian, but that is not tested or supported.
  #6 24.87 
  #6 24.87 Packages
  #6 24.87 ========
  #6 24.87 
  #6 24.87 The packages provided here are loosely based on the debian upstream packages with some modifications to make them more usable as non-default pythons and on ubuntu.  As such, the packages follow debian's patterns and often do not include a full python distribution with just `apt install python#.#`.  Here is a list of packages that may be useful along with the default install:
  #6 24.87 
  #6 24.87 - `python#.#-dev`: includes development headers for building C extensions
  #6 24.87 - `python#.#-venv`: provides the standard library `venv` module
  #6 24.87 - `python#.#-distutils`: provides the standard library `distutils` module
  #6 24.87 - `python#.#-lib2to3`: provides the `2to3-#.#` utility as well as the standard library `lib2to3` module
  #6 24.87 - `python#.#-gdbm`: provides the standard library `dbm.gnu` module
  #6 24.87 - `python#.#-tk`: provides the standard library `tkinter` module
  #6 24.87 
  #6 24.87 Third-Party Python Modules
  #6 24.87 ==========================
  #6 24.87 
  #6 24.87 Python modules in the official Ubuntu repositories are packaged to work with the Python interpreters from the official repositories. Accordingly, they generally won't work with the Python interpreters from this PPA. As an exception, pure-Python modules for Python 3 will work, but any compiled extension modules won't.
  #6 24.87 
  #6 24.87 To install 3rd-party Python modules, you should use the common Python packaging tools.  For an introduction into the Python packaging ecosystem and its tools, refer to the Python Packaging User Guide:
  #6 24.87 https://packaging.python.org/installing/
  #6 24.87

  #6 24.87 https://github.com/deadsnakes/

DOCKERFILE:
  # Stage 1: Base image with common dependencies and project source
  FROM ubuntu:22.04 AS base
  # Avoid interactive prompts during build
  ENV DEBIAN_FRONTEND=noninteractive
  # Install common system dependencies, build tools, and Python 3.7
  RUN apt-get update && \
      apt-get install -y --no-install-recommends \
      # For adding PPA repository
      software-properties-common \
      # Version control and networking tools
      git \
      curl \
      nmap \
      iproute2 \
      # Build essentials and compiler tools
      build-essential \
      bison \
      flex \
      libfl-dev \
      && add-apt-repository -y ppa:deadsnakes/ppa && \
      apt-get update && \
      # Install Python 3.7 and its development files
      apt-get install -y --no-install-recommends python3.7 python3.7-distutils python3.7-dev && \
      # Clean up APT cache to reduce image size
      apt-get clean && \
      rm -rf /var/lib/apt/lists/*
  # Install pip for Python 3.7
  RUN curl https://bootstrap.pypa.io/get-pip.py -o get-pip.py && \
      python3.7 get-pip.py && \
      rm get-pip.py
  # Install required Python libraries
  RUN python3.7 -m pip install --no-cache-dir scapy==2.4.5
  # Set the working directory
  WORKDIR /app
  # Copy the project source code into the image
  COPY . .
  # Build the netcl policy compiler
  RUN cd compiler && make netcl
  # Stage 2: Switch image prepared for Tofino SDE
  FROM base AS switch
  # Set environment variables for Tofino SDE for consistency with the plan
  ENV SDE=/root/bf-sde-9.7.0
  ENV SDE_INSTALL=${SDE}/install
  ENV PATH=${SDE_INSTALL}/bin:${PATH}
  ENV LD_LIBRARY_PATH=${SDE_INSTALL}/lib:${LD_LIBRARY_PATH}
  # --- Tofino SDE Installation Placeholder ---
  # The Tofino SDE is proprietary and must be obtained from Intel.
  # It is assumed to be present in the build context if needed.
  # To install, place the SDE archive in the project root and uncomment the following:
  #
  # COPY bf-sde-9.7.0.tar.gz /root/
  # RUN cd /root && \
  #     tar -xf bf-sde-9.7.0.tar.gz && \
  #     rm bf-sde-9.7.0.tar.gz && \
  #     cd ${SDE} && \
  #     ./p4studio_build/p4studio_build.py --use-profile p416_examples.pro
  # Set the working directory to the root of the repository
  WORKDIR /app
  # Start a bash shell when the container is run
  CMD ["/bin/bash"]
  # Stage 3: Host image with eBPF/BCC tools (Default Target)
  FROM base AS host
  # Install eBPF/BCC tools
  RUN apt-get update && \
      apt-get install -y --no-install-recommends \
      bpfcc-tools \
      libbpfcc-dev \
      && apt-get clean && \
      rm -rf /var/lib/apt/lists/*
  # Set the working directory to the root of the repository
  WORKDIR /app
  # Start a bash shell when the container is run
  CMD ["/bin/bash"]
--- End of Iteration 4 ---

=== Iteration 5 - [2025-08-28 02:21:09] ===
PLAN:
  Based on the provided hardware and environment information, which strongly indicates a containerized setup using Docker, the original plan requires significant adjustments to ensure feasibility. The following revised plan is tailored for an `x86_64` architecture using Docker containers on a Linux host, replacing physical multi-host dependencies with a simulated container network and a software switch model instead of hardware drivers.
  ***
  ### **ADJUSTED ENVIRONMENT SETUP PLAN**
  **Context:** This plan is adapted for a containerized environment managed by Docker. The "Switch Management Machine" and "Hosts" (Host1, Host2, Host3) will be run as separate Docker containers. The working directory `/home/cc/EnvGym/data/P4Ctl` is the Docker build context.
  1.  DOWNLOADS NEEDED:
      *   **Base Docker Image:** `ubuntu:22.04` (LTS). This is recommended over 20.04 to ensure a more recent host kernel is available, which is critical for eBPF/BCC compatibility with kernel versions like 5.15.0+. Docker containers share the host's kernel.
      *   **P4 Switch Software:** Tofino Switch SDE 9.7.0 (Requires access from Intel/Barefoot). For this containerized environment, we will use the **Tofino behavioral model (`modeld`)** included in the SDE, not the physical hardware driver (`switchd`).
      *   **eBPF Toolchain:** BCC (Bionic Compiler Collection). Must be compatible with the **host machine's Linux Kernel**.
      *   **Programming Language:** Python 3.7.
      *   **Python Libraries:** Scapy 2.4.5.
      *   **Compiler Tools:** Bison 3.8.2, Flex 2.6.4, `g++` (from `build-essential`), `libfl-dev`.
      *   **Networking Tools:** `ncat` (from `nmap`), `iproute2` (for `ip a`).
      *   **Source Code:** The P4Control project repository from `https://github.com/peng-gao-lab/p4control`.
  2.  FILES TO CREATE/MODIFY (Within the Container Filesystem):
      *   **File to Modify:** `host_agent/host_agent.py`
          *   **Path:** Within the cloned `p4control` repository, on each of the three "host" containers.
          *   **Description:** This file must be edited to specify the correct network interface name. In a standard Docker container network, this is typically **`"eth0"`**. Search for the interface name variable and update its value accordingly.
      *   **File to Modify (Dynamically):** `host_agent/host_agent_ebpf.c`
          *   **Path:** Within the cloned `p4control` repository, on each of the three "host" containers.
          *   **Description:** Before running the host agent, the `TAGGED_TERMINAL` macro must be updated with the PID of the shell process *inside the specific container*. This is found by running `ps` after attaching to the container's shell.
      *   **File to Modify (for Custom Policies):** `switch/netcl.py`
          *   **Path:** Within the cloned `p4control` repository, in the "switch" container.
          *   **Description:** To apply custom network policies, compile them using the `netcl-compile` tool. The output must be copied into this Python file, replacing the existing rules.
      *   **File to Create (Executable):** `compiler/netcl-compile`
          *   **Path:** Within the cloned `p4control` repository, in the `compiler/` subdirectory inside the "switch" container.
          *   **Description:** This compiler executable is built from source using the provided Makefile. It must be built before the switch controller can be run with custom policies.
  3.  NECESSARY TEST CASES IN THE CODEBASE:
      *   **(No changes)** The logic of the test cases remains the same, but they will be executed between containers on a Docker network instead of between physical hosts.
  4.  COMPLETE TODO LIST:
      *   **Phase 1: Docker Image and Environment Preparation (On Host Machine)**
          1.  **Create a Dockerfile:** In a new directory, create a `Dockerfile` to build a base image with all common dependencies.
              ```Dockerfile
              # Use Ubuntu 22.04 for better kernel compatibility for eBPF
              FROM ubuntu:22.04
              # Avoid interactive prompts during build
              ENV DEBIAN_FRONTEND=noninteractive
              # Install common dependencies and add repository for Python 3.7
              RUN apt-get update && \
                  apt-get install -y software-properties-common && \
                  add-apt-repository ppa:deadsnakes/ppa && \
                  apt-get update && \
                  apt-get install -y git python3.7 python3.7-distutils python3.7-dev nmap build-essential libfl-dev iproute2 curl && \
                  rm -rf /var/lib/apt/lists/*
              # Install pip for Python 3.7
              RUN curl https://bootstrap.pypa.io/get-pip.py -o get-pip.py && \
                  python3.7 get-pip.py && \
                  rm get-pip.py
              # Install required Python library
              RUN python3.7 -m pip install scapy==2.4.5
              # Set a working directory
              WORKDIR /root
              ```
          2.  **Build the Base Docker Image:**
              ```bash
              docker build -t p4control-base .
              ```
          3.  **Prepare Project and SDE:**
              *   Clone the P4Control project into the build context directory: `git clone https://github.com/peng-gao-lab/p4control /home/cc/EnvGym/data/P4Ctl`.
              *   Download and extract the Tofino SDE 9.7.0 into the build context as well, so it can be copied into the switch container.
          4.  **Create Docker Network:** Create a dedicated network for the containers to communicate.
              ```bash
              docker network create --subnet=10.0.0.0/24 p4control-net
              ```
      *   **Phase 2: Launch Containers**
          1.  **Launch the Switch Container:** This container will run the Tofino model and the controller.
              ```bash
              docker run -itd --name p4switch --net p4control-net -v /home/cc/EnvGym/data/P4Ctl:/root/p4control --cap-add=ALL --privileged p4control-base
              ```
          2.  **Launch the Host Containers:**
              ```bash
              docker run -itd --name host1 --net p4control-net --ip 10.0.0.1 -v /home/cc/EnvGym/data/P4Ctl:/root/p4control --cap-add=ALL --privileged p4control-base
              docker run -itd --name host2 --net p4control-net --ip 10.0.0.2 -v /home/cc/EnvGym/data/P4Ctl:/root/p4control --cap-add=ALL --privileged p4control-base
              docker run -itd --name host3 --net p4control-net --ip 10.0.0.3 -v /home/cc/EnvGym/data/P4Ctl:/root/p4control --cap-add=ALL --privileged p4control-base
              ```
          3.  **Verification:**
              ```bash
              docker ps # Should show p4switch, host1, host2, and host3 running
              ```
      *   **Phase 3: Tofino SDE and Host Environment Setup**
          1.  **On the Switch Container (`p4switch`):**
              *   Copy the SDE into the container (if not mounted via volume) and install it according to vendor instructions.
              *   Set environment variables. It's best to do this by attaching to the container:
                  ```bash
                  docker exec -it p4switch bash
                  # Inside the container:
                  echo 'export SDE=/path/to/bf-sde-9.7.0/' >> ~/.bashrc
                  echo 'export SDE_INSTALL=/path/to/bf-sde-9.7.0/install' >> ~/.bashrc
                  source ~/.bashrc
                  exit
                  ```
          2.  **On Each Host Container (`host1`, `host2`, `host3`):**
              *   Attach to the container: `docker exec -it <container_name> bash`.
              *   Install build tools (Bison, Flex) and BCC as described in the original plan. The host's kernel must be compatible.
              *   Configure Host Agent: Edit `/root/p4control/host_agent/host_agent.py` and set the interface name to `"eth0"`.
      *   **Phase 4: Build P4 Program and Start Switch Simulator (in `p4switch` container)**
          1.  Attach to the switch container: `docker exec -it p4switch bash`.
          2.  Navigate to the project directory: `cd /root/p4control`.
          3.  Build the P4 program: `./p4_build.sh -p switch/p4control.p4`.
          4.  Run the **Tofino behavioral model** in the background.
              ```bash
              ./run_tofino_model.sh -p p4control &
              ```
          5.  **Verification:** The model should be running without errors.
      *   **Phase 5: Compile Policy and Run Controller (in `p4switch` container)**
          1.  While still inside the `p4switch` container, navigate to `compiler`: `cd compiler`.
          2.  Build the policy compiler: `make netcl`.
          3.  Compile the policy and copy the output rules.
          4.  Paste the new rules into `switch/netcl.py`.
          5.  Navigate to the project root and start the controller:
              ```bash
              cd ..
              python3.7 switch/controller.py
              ```
          6.  **Verification:** The controller should log its connection to the switch model and the insertion of rules.
      *   **Phase 6: Deploy Host Agents (in `host1`, `host2`, `host3` containers)**
          1.  For each host container (e.g., `host1`):
              *   Attach an interactive shell: `docker exec -it host1 bash`.
              *   Get the PID of this shell: `ps`. Note the PID for the `bash` process.
              *   Edit `/root/p4control/host_agent/host_agent_ebpf.c` and set `TAGGED_TERMINAL` to this PID.
              *   In the same shell, run the agent: `sudo python3.7 host_agent/host_agent.py`.
          2.  **Verification:** The agent should start without eBPF compilation or attachment errors.
          3.  Repeat this process for `host2` and `host3` in separate terminal windows.
      *   **Phase 7: Execute Verification Test Case**
          1.  **On Host2 and Host3:** In the shells where the agents are running, start `ncat` listeners.
              ```bash
              # In host2's attached shell
              sudo ncat -nlvp 9999 -e /bin/bash
              # In host3's attached shell
              sudo ncat -nlvp 9999 -e /bin/bash
              ```
          2.  **On Host1:** In its attached shell, connect to Host2.
              ```bash
              sudo ncat 10.0.0.2 9999
              ```
          3.  **Verification:** You should get a shell prompt from Host2 inside the Host1 terminal.
          4.  **From the session on Host1 (now connected to Host2):** Attempt to connect to Host3.
              ```bash
              ncat 10.0.0.3 9999
              ```
          5.  **Final Verification:** This connection must fail (hang or timeout). This confirms the P4Control policy, enforced by the Tofino model, has correctly blocked the prohibited information flow between containers.
NEXT:
  current progress

This Dockerfile correctly installs system dependencies and Python 3.7.   #6 27.85 Supported Ubuntu and Python Versions
  #6 27.85 ====================================
  #6 27.85 
  #6 27.85 - Ubuntu 20.04 (focal) Python3.5 - Python3.7, Python3.9 - Python3.13
  #6 27.85 - Ubuntu 22.04 (jammy) Python3.7 - Python3.9, Python3.11 - Python3.13
  #6 27.85 - Ubuntu 24.04 (noble) Python3.7 - Python3.11, Python3.13
  #6 27.85 - Note: Python2.7 (focal, jammy), Python 3.8 (focal), Python 3.10 (jammy), Python3.12 (noble) are not provided by deadsnakes as upstream ubuntu provides those packages.
  #6 27.85 
  #6 27.85 Why some packages aren't built:
  #6 27.85 - Note: for focal, older python versions require libssl<1.1 so they are not currently built
  #6 27.85 - Note: for jammy and noble, older python versions requre libssl<3 so they are not currently built
  #6 27.85 - If you need these, reach out to asottile to set up a private ppa
  #6 27.85 
  #6 27.85 The packages may also work on other versions of Ubuntu or Debian, but that is not tested or supported.
  #6 27.85 
  #6 27.85 Packages
  #6 27.85 ========
  #6 27.85 
  #6 27.85 The packages provided here are loosely based on the debian upstream packages with some modifications to make them more usable as non-default pythons and on ubuntu.  As such, the packages follow debian's patterns and often do not include a full python distribution with just `apt install python#.#`.  Here is a list of packages that may be useful along with the default install:
  #6 27.85 
  #6 27.85 - `python#.#-dev`: includes development headers for building C extensions
  #6 27.85 - `python#.#-venv`: provides the standard library `venv` module
  #6 27.85 - `python#.#-distutils`: provides the standard library `distutils` module
  #6 27.85 - `python#.#-lib2to3`: provides the `2to3-#.#` utility as well as the standard library `lib2to3` module
  #6 27.85 - `python#.#-gdbm`: provides the standard library `dbm.gnu` module
  #6 27.85 - `python#.#-tk`: provides the standard library `tkinter` module
  #6 27.85 
  #6 27.85 Third-Party Python Modules
  #6 27.85 ==========================
  #6 27.85 
  #6 27.85 Python modules in the official Ubuntu repositories are packaged to work with the Python interpreters from the official repositories. Accordingly, they generally won't work with the Python interpreters from this PPA. As an exception, pure-Python modules for Python 3 will work, but any compiled extension modules won't.
  #6 27.85 
  #6 27.85 To install 3rd-party Python modules, you should use the common Python packaging tools.  For an introduction into the Python packaging ecosystem and its tools, refer to the Python Packaging User Guide:
  #6 27.85 https://packaging.python.org/installing/
